[L8] -- ============================================================================ [L9] [L10] -- Contacts table (individuals at companies) [L11] CREATE TABLE contacts ( [L12] id UUID PRIMARY KEY DEFAULT uuid_generate_v4(), [L13] org_id UUID REFERENCES organizations(id) ON DELETE CASCADE, [L14] first_name VARCHAR(100) NOT NULL, [L15] last_name VARCHAR(100) NOT NULL, [L16] email VARCHAR(255), [L17] phone VARCHAR(20), [L18] phone_ext VARCHAR(10), [L19] mobile VARCHAR(20), [L20] title VARCHAR(100), -- Job title [L21] role VARCHAR(50) CHECK (role IN ( [L22] 'owner', 'ceo', 'cfo', 'controller', 'manager', 'bookkeeper', 'other' [L23] )), [L24] preferred_contact_method VARCHAR(20) DEFAULT 'email' CHECK (preferred_contact_method IN ( [L25] 'email', 'phone', 'mobile', 'sms' [L26] )), [L27] timezone VARCHAR(50) DEFAULT 'America/New_York', [L28] notes TEXT, [L29] tags VARCHAR(50)[] DEFAULT '{}', [L30] source VARCHAR(50), -- Where the contact came from [L31] is_active BOOLEAN DEFAULT true, [L32] last_contacted_at TIMESTAMP WITH TIME ZONE, [L33] created_by UUID REFERENCES users(id), [L34] created_at TIMESTAMP WITH TIME ZONE DEFAULT NOW(), [L35] updated_at TIMESTAMP WITH TIME ZONE DEFAULT NOW() [L36] ); [L37] [L38] CREATE INDEX idx_contacts_org ON contacts(org_id); [L39] CREATE INDEX idx_contacts_email ON contacts(email); [L40] CREATE INDEX idx_contacts_phone ON contacts(phone); [L41] CREATE INDEX idx_contacts_name ON contacts(last_name, first_name); [L42] CREATE INDEX idx_contacts_tags ON contacts USING gin(tags); [L43] CREATE INDEX idx_contacts_active ON contacts(org_id, is_active) WHERE is_active = true; [L44] [L45] -- Junction table: Prospects <-> Contacts (many-to-many) [L46] CREATE TABLE prospect_contacts ( [L47] id UUID PRIMARY KEY DEFAULT uuid_generate_v4(), [L48] prospect_id UUID REFERENCES prospects(id) ON DELETE CASCADE, [L49] contact_id UUID REFERENCES contacts(id) ON DELETE CASCADE, [L50] is_primary BOOLEAN DEFAULT false, [L51] relationship VARCHAR(50) DEFAULT 'employee' CHECK (relationship IN ( [L52] 'owner', 'decision_maker', 'influencer', 'employee', 'advisor', 'other' [L53] )), [L54] created_at TIMESTAMP WITH TIME ZONE DEFAULT NOW(), [L55] [L56] CONSTRAINT unique_prospect_contact UNIQUE (prospect_id, contact_id) [L57] ); [L58] [L59] CREATE INDEX idx_prospect_contacts_prospect ON prospect_contacts(prospect_id); [L60] CREATE INDEX idx_prospect_contacts_contact ON prospect_contacts(contact_id); [L61] CREATE INDEX idx_prospect_contacts_primary ON prospect_contacts(prospect_id, is_primary) [L62] WHERE is_primary = true; [L63] [L64] -- Contact activities (interactions log) [L65] CREATE TABLE contact_activities ( [L66] id UUID PRIMARY KEY DEFAULT uuid_generate_v4(), [L67] contact_id UUID REFERENCES contacts(id) ON DELETE CASCADE, [L68] prospect_id UUID REFERENCES prospects(id) ON DELETE SET NULL, [L69] user_id UUID REFERENCES users(id) ON DELETE SET NULL, [L70] activity_type VARCHAR(30) NOT NULL CHECK (activity_type IN ( [L71] 'call_outbound', 'call_inbound', 'call_missed', [L72] 'email_sent', 'email_received', 'email_opened', 'email_clicked', [L73] 'sms_sent', 'sms_received', [L74] 'meeting_scheduled', 'meeting_completed', 'meeting_cancelled', [L75] 'note', 'task_created', 'task_completed', [L76] 'status_change', 'document_sent', 'document_signed' [L77] )), [L78] subject VARCHAR(255), [L79] description TEXT, [L80] outcome VARCHAR(50), -- e.g., 'interested', 'not_interested', 'callback', 'voicemail' [L81] duration_seconds INTEGER, -- For calls [L82] metadata JSONB DEFAULT '{}', -- Additional activity-specific data [L83] scheduled_at TIMESTAMP WITH TIME ZONE, -- For scheduled activities [L84] completed_at TIMESTAMP WITH TIME ZONE, [L85] created_at TIMESTAMP WITH TIME ZONE DEFAULT NOW() [L86] ); [L87] [L88] CREATE INDEX idx_contact_activities_contact ON contact_activities(contact_id); [L89] CREATE INDEX idx_contact_activities_prospect ON contact_activities(prospect_id); [L90] CREATE INDEX idx_contact_activities_user ON contact_activities(user_id); [L91] CREATE INDEX idx_contact_activities_type ON contact_activities(activity_type); [L92] CREATE INDEX idx_contact_activities_created ON contact_activities(created_at DESC); [L93] [L94] -- Ensure only one primary contact per prospect [L95] CREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION ensure_single_primary_contact() [L96] RETURNS TRIGGER AS $$ [L97] BEGIN [L98] IF NEW.is_primary = true THEN [L99] UPDATE prospect_contacts [L100] SET is_primary = false [L101] WHERE prospect_id = NEW.prospect_id [L102] AND id != NEW.id [L103] AND is_primary = true; [L104] END IF; [L105] RETURN NEW; [L106] END; [L107] $$ LANGUAGE plpgsql; [L108] [L109] CREATE TRIGGER enforce_single_primary_contact [L110] BEFORE INSERT OR UPDATE OF is_primary ON prospect_contacts [L111] FOR EACH ROW [L112] WHEN (NEW.is_primary = true) [L113] EXECUTE FUNCTION ensure_single_primary_contact(); [L114] [L115] -- Update last_contacted_at on contact when activity is logged [L116] CREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION update_contact_last_contacted() [L117] RETURNS TRIGGER AS $$ [L118] BEGIN [L119] IF NEW.activity_type IN ('call_outbound', 'call_inbound', 'email_sent', 'sms_sent', 'meeting_completed') THEN [L120] UPDATE contacts [L121] SET last_contacted_at = NEW.created_at [L122] WHERE id = NEW.contact_id; [L123] END IF; [L124] RETURN NEW; [L125] END; [L126] $$ LANGUAGE plpgsql; [L127] [L128] CREATE TRIGGER update_contact_last_contacted_trigger [L129] AFTER INSERT ON contact_activities [L130] FOR EACH ROW [L131] EXECUTE FUNCTION update_contact_last_contacted(); [L132] [L133] -- Update timestamps [L134] CREATE TRIGGER update_contacts_updated_at [L135] BEFORE UPDATE ON contacts [L136] FOR EACH ROW [L137] EXECUTE FUNCTION update_updated_at(); [L138] [L139] -- Comments [L140] COMMENT ON TABLE contacts IS 'Individual contacts associated with prospects/companies'; [L141] COMMENT ON TABLE prospect_contacts IS 'Junction table linking prospects to their contacts'; [L142] COMMENT ON TABLE contact_activities IS 'Log of all interactions with contacts';

Citation Marker: fileciteturn83file0 [L1] encoding: utf-8 [L2] sha: 8165432a02a365162e5e89982dc05930a4943626 [L3] content: --- [L4] name: networking-outreach [L5] description: Build professional relationships through strategic outreach—cold emails, LinkedIn engagement, informational interviews, and follow-up sequences. Authentic connection over transactional networking. Triggers on networking, cold outreach, LinkedIn strategy, or informational interview requests. [L6] license: MIT [L7] governance_phases: [ship] [L8] triggers: [user-asks-about-networking, user-asks-about-outreach, user-asks-about-linkedin] [L9] complements: [content-distribution, portfolio-presentation, github-profile-architect] [L10] --- [L11] [L12] # Networking Outreach [L13] [L14] Build genuine professional relationships at scale. [L15] [L16] ## Networking Philosophy [L17] [L18] ### The Mindset Shift [L19] [L20] | Transactional | Relational | [L21] |---------------|------------| [L22] | "What can you do for me?" | "How can I be useful?" | [L23] | One-time ask | Ongoing relationship | [L24] | Immediate need | Long-term investment | [L25] | Extract value | Create value | [L26] [L27] ### The Give-First Principle [L28] [L29] Before asking for anything: [L30] - Share relevant content [L31] - Make introductions [L32] - Offer help or expertise [L33] - Engage with their work [L34] [L35] --- [L36] [L37] ## Outreach Strategy [L38] [L39] ### Target Identification [L40] [L41] | Category | Who | Why | [L42] |----------|-----|-----| [L43] | **Direct targets** | Hiring managers, recruiters | Decision makers | [L44] | **Warm connections** | Alumni, former colleagues | Shared context | [L45] | **Industry peers** | Similar role, different company | Mutual learning | [L46] | **Thought leaders** | Content creators, speakers | Visibility + learning | [L47] | **Connectors** | Well-networked individuals | Access to network | [L48] [L49] ### Research Before Outreach [L50] [L51] For each person: [L52] - Current role and company [L53] - Career path [L54] - Shared connections [L55] - Recent content/achievements [L56] - Potential common ground [L57] [L58] --- [L59] [L60] ## Cold Email Framework [L61] [L62] ### The AIDA Structure [L63] [L64] ``` [L65] Attention: Hook that earns the read [L66] Interest: Why you're reaching out [L67] Desire: What's in it for them / credibility [L68] Action: Clear, easy ask [L69] ``` [L70] [L71] ### Cold Email Template [L72] [L73] ``` [L74] Subject: [Specific, relevant, not clickbait] [L75] [L76] Hi [Name], [L77] [L78] [One sentence showing you did research—specific to them] [L79] [L80] [Why you're reaching out—be direct] [L81] [L82] [Brief credibility—why you, why now] [L83] [L84] [Specific, low-commitment ask] [L85] [L86] [Graceful out—acknowledge they're busy] [L87] [L88] Best, [L89] [Your name] [L90] [One-line signature] [L91] ``` [L92] [L93] ### Example: Informational Interview Request [L94] [L95] ``` [L96] Subject: Quick question about [their specialty] at [Company] [L97] [L98] Hi Sarah, [L99] [L100] I came across your post about migrating to microservices at Stripe— [L101] the part about managing tech debt during the transition resonated [L102] with challenges I'm facing. [L103] [L104] I'm a senior engineer exploring platform roles, and Stripe's [L105] infrastructure work is particularly interesting to me. [L106] [L107] Would you have 20 minutes for a call? I'd love to hear how you [L108] approached [specific thing]. Happy to work around your schedule. [L109] [L110] No worries if you're swamped—I know these requests add up. [L111] [L112] Best, [L113] [Name] [L114] ``` [L115] [L116] ### Subject Line Patterns [L117] [L118] | Pattern | Example | [L119] |---------|---------| [L120] | Mutual connection | "Alex Chen suggested I reach out" | [L121] | Specific reference | "Your talk on X at Y" | [L122] | Direct ask | "Quick question about [topic]" | [L123] | Shared context | "Fellow [school] alum in [field]" | [L124] | Value offer | "Resource on [topic you discussed]" | [L125] [L126] ### What NOT to Do [L127] [L128] ❌ Generic templates with no personalization [L129] ❌ Long emails (>150 words for cold) [L130] ❌ Asking for a job directly [L131] ❌ No clear ask [L132] ❌ Attachments on first email [L133] ❌ Following up aggressively [L134] [L135] --- [L136] [L137] ## LinkedIn Strategy [L138] [L139] ### Profile Optimization [L140] [L141] - **Headline**: Not just title—value proposition [L142] - **About**: First person, story-driven, keywords [L143] - **Experience**: Accomplishments, not duties [L144] - **Featured**: Best work, portfolio links [L145] - **Activity**: Regular engagement [L146] [L147] ### Connection Requests [L148] [L149] ``` [L150] Hi [Name], [L151] [L152] [One sentence of context—how you found them, what you have in common] [L153] [L154] [Why you want to connect—specific, genuine] [L155] [L156] [Name] [L157] ``` [L158] [L159] **Example**: [L160] ``` [L161] Hi Marcus, [L162] [L163] I saw your comment on Lenny's post about PLG metrics—your point [L164] about activation vs. engagement really clarified something I've [L165] been wrestling with. [L166] [L167] Would love to connect and follow your thinking on product growth. [L168] [L169] [Name] [L170] ``` [L171] [L172] ### Engagement Strategy [L173] [L174] **Daily** (5-10 min): [L175] - Comment thoughtfully on 2-3 posts [L176] - React to content from targets [L177] [L178] **Weekly** (30 min): [L179] - Post original content or insight [L180] - Send 3-5 connection requests [L181] - Message 2-3 existing connections [L182] [L183] **Quality Comments**: [L184] - Add insight, not just agreement [L185] - Ask thoughtful questions [L186] - Share relevant experience [L187] - Tag when genuinely relevant [L188] [L189] --- [L190] [L191] ## Informational Interviews [L192] [L193] ### The Ask [L194] [L195] Keep it specific and low-commitment: [L196] - 15-20 minutes (not 30) [L197] - Phone/video (their preference) [L198] - Flexible on timing [L199] - Clear topic [L200] [L201] ### Preparation [L202] [L203] - Research their background thoroughly [L204] - Prepare 5-7 questions [L205] - Know what you want to learn [L206] - Have your own story ready [L207] [L208] ### Question Framework [L209] [L210] **Career Path**: [L211] - "How did you get into [field]?" [L212] - "What led you from [A] to [B]?" [L213] [L214] **Role Insight**: [L215] - "What does a typical week look like?" [L216] - "What surprised you about this role?" [L217] [L218] **Industry/Company**: [L219] - "What trends are you watching?" [L220] - "What's the culture really like?" [L221] [L222] **Advice**: [L223] - "What would you do differently?" [L224] - "What should I be learning?" [L225] [L226] **Closing**: [L227] - "Who else should I talk to?" [L228] - "How can I be helpful to you?" [L229] [L230] ### During the Call [L231] [L232] - Be on time (early) [L233] - Let them talk (80/20) [L234] - Take notes [L235] - Watch the time [L236] - Ask for referrals naturally [L237] - Offer value if you can [L238] [L239] ### After the Call [L240] [L241] - Thank you email within 24 hours [L242] - Connect on LinkedIn if not already [L243] - Follow up on anything discussed [L244] - Stay in touch (content shares, updates) [L245] [L246] --- [L247] [L248] ## Follow-Up Sequences [L249] [L250] ### After No Response (Cold) [L251] [L252] ``` [L253] Day 0: Initial email [L254] Day 4-5: Bump email [L255] Day 10-14: Final follow-up with new angle [L256] ``` [L257] [L258] **Bump Email**: [L259] ``` [L260] Subject: Re: [original subject] [L261] [L262] Hi [Name], [L263] [L264] Just floating this back up in case it got buried. [L265] [L266] [One new sentence of value or context] [L267] [L268] [Name] [L269] ``` [L270] [L271] **Final Follow-Up**: [L272] ``` [L273] Subject: Re: [original subject] [L274] [L275] Hi [Name], [L276] [L277] I'll assume now isn't a good time. No worries at all. [L278] [L279] If things change, I'd still love to connect about [topic]. [L280] [L281] Best, [L282] [Name] [L283] ``` [L284] [L285] ### After Informational Interview [L286] [L287] ``` [L288] Day 0: Thank you email [L289] Week 2-4: Share relevant article/resource [L290] Month 1-2: Update on your progress [L291] Ongoing: Engage with their content [L292] ``` [L293] [L294] ### After Job Application [L295] [L296] ``` [L297] Day 0: Apply [L298] Day 3-5: Reach out to hiring manager/recruiter [L299] Day 10: Follow up if no response [L300] Post-interview: Same day thank you [L301] ``` [L302] [L303] --- [L304] [L305] ## Tracking System [L306] [L307] ### Simple Spreadsheet [L308] [L309] | Name | Company | How Found | Status | Last Contact | Next Action | Notes | [L310] |------|---------|-----------|--------|--------------|-------------|-------| [L311] | [Name] | [Co] | [Source] | [Stage] | [Date] | [Action] | [Notes] | [L312] [L313] ### Status Stages [L314] [L315] - Researching [L316] - Outreach sent [L317] - Replied [L318] - Scheduled [L319] - Completed [L320] - Follow-up due [L321] - Warm contact [L322] [L323] --- [L324] [L325] ## References [L326] [L327] - `references/email-templates.md` - Full template library [L328] - `references/linkedin-scripts.md` - Connection and message templates [L329] - `references/tracking-template.md` - CRM spreadsheet

Citation Marker: fileciteturn84file0 [L1] encoding: utf-8 [L2] sha: 176134040f84c0801bd404b297fbb251026108e7 [L3] content: --- [L4] name: content-distribution [L5] description: Promote creative and technical work through strategic content distribution. Covers platform selection, audience building, content repurposing, and engagement strategies without becoming a full-time marketer. Triggers on promotion, audience building, social media strategy, or content marketing requests. [L6] license: MIT [L7] governance_phases: [ship] [L8] governance_norm_group: distribution-readiness [L9] organ_affinity: [organ-vii] [L10] triggers: [user-asks-about-promotion, user-asks-about-content-strategy, context:distribution] [L11] complements: [portfolio-presentation, networking-outreach, github-profile-architect] [L12] --- [L13] [L14] # Content Distribution [L15] [L16] Get your work seen without becoming a full-time marketer. [L17] [L18] ## Distribution Philosophy [L19] [L20] ### The Reality [L21] [L22] - Great work doesn't promote itself [L23] - You don't need millions of followers [L24] - Consistency beats virality [L25] - Value attracts audience [L26] [L27] ### The Sustainable Approach [L28] [L29] | Unsustainable | Sustainable | [L30] |---------------|-------------| [L31] | Post daily everywhere | Focus on 1-2 platforms | [L32] | Chase trends | Build on your expertise | [L33] | Optimize for algorithm | Optimize for humans | [L34] | Content for content's sake | Share genuine value | [L35] [L36] --- [L37] [L38] ## Platform Selection [L39] [L40] ### Choose Based On [L41] [L42] 1. **Where is your audience?** [L43] 2. **What format fits your work?** [L44] 3. **What can you sustain?** [L45] [L46] ### Platform Strengths [L47] [L48] | Platform | Best For | Content Type | Effort | [L49] |----------|----------|--------------|--------| [L50] | Twitter/X | Tech, ideas, discussion | Short-form, threads | Medium | [L51] | LinkedIn | Professional, B2B | Articles, updates | Medium | [L52] | Instagram | Visual work, creative | Images, reels | High | [L53] | YouTube | Tutorials, long-form | Video | Very High | [L54] | TikTok | Entertainment, quick tips | Short video | High | [L55] | Substack/Newsletter | Deep content, owned audience | Long-form writing | Medium | [L56] | Personal Blog | SEO, portfolio | Any | Low | [L57] | GitHub | Code, open source | Repositories | Low | [L58] [L59] ### The 70/20/10 Rule [L60] [L61] Pick ONE primary platform: [L62] - 70% of effort on primary platform [L63] - 20% on secondary platform [L64] - 10% experimenting [L65] [L66] --- [L67] [L68] ## Content Strategy [L69] [L70] ### Content Pillars [L71] [L72] Define 3-5 themes you consistently create around: [L73] [L74] ``` [L75] Example for a creative technologist: [L76] 1. Technical tutorials (how I built X) [L77] 2. Creative process (behind the scenes) [L78] 3. Industry commentary (trends, tools) [L79] 4. Personal projects (show the work) [L80] 5. Career/professional development [L81] ``` [L82] [L83] ### Content Types by Effort [L84] [L85] | Low Effort | Medium Effort | High Effort | [L86] |------------|---------------|-------------| [L87] | Retweet + comment | Thread/carousel | Blog post | [L88] | Quick tip | Short-form video | YouTube video | [L89] | Question | Newsletter | Course/workshop | [L90] | Work-in-progress | Case study | Open source project | [L91] | Curated links | Tutorial | Research paper | [L92] [L93] ### The 4-1-1 Rule [L94] [L95] For every 6 posts: [L96] - 4 share value from others (curate) [L97] - 1 soft self-promotion [L98] - 1 direct self-promotion [L99] [L100] Or: **Give value 5x for every 1x you ask** [L101] [L102] --- [L103] [L104] ## Content Creation [L105] [L106] ### The Show Your Work Framework [L107] [L108] From Austin Kleon: [L109] [L110] 1. **Daily dispatch**: Share process, not just product [L111] 2. **Flow, not stock**: Ongoing sharing, not just launches [L112] 3. **Become a documentarian**: Capture as you go [L113] [L114] ### Content Prompts [L115] [L116] **Process**: [L117] - What are you working on today? [L118] - What problem did you just solve? [L119] - What mistake did you make? [L120] - What did you learn this week? [L121] [L122] **Teaching**: [L123] - What do beginners get wrong? [L124] - What's a shortcut you discovered? [L125] - What tool changed your workflow? [L126] - What concept took you too long to understand? [L127] [L128] **Opinion**: [L129] - What's a hot take in your field? [L130] - What's underrated/overrated? [L131] - What would you tell yourself 5 years ago? [L132] - What do you disagree with experts on? [L133] [L134] ### Writing Formats That Work [L135] [L136] **Thread/Carousel**: [L137] ``` [L138] Hook: Surprising claim or question [L139] Point 1: [Evidence/example] [L140] Point 2: [Evidence/example] [L141] Point 3: [Evidence/example] [L142] Summary: Key takeaway [L143] CTA: Follow for more / Link to resource [L144] ``` [L145] [L146] **Short-form post**: [L147] ``` [L148] [Hook - first line matters most] [L149] [L150] [Value - the actual content] [L151] [L152] [CTA - what to do next] [L153] ``` [L154] [L155] --- [L156] [L157] ## Repurposing [L158] [L159] ### The Content Pyramid [L160] [L161] ``` [L162] ┌───────────┐ [L163] │ Pillar │ Long-form (blog, video) [L164] │ Content │ [L165] └─────┬─────┘ [L166] │ [L167] ┌───────────┼───────────┐ [L168] ▼ ▼ ▼ [L169] ┌────────┐ ┌────────┐ ┌────────┐ [L170] │Thread 1│ │Thread 2│ │Thread 3│ Medium-form [L171] └────┬───┘ └────┬───┘ └────┬───┘ [L172] │ │ │ [L173] ┌────┴────┬─────┴────┬─────┴────┐ [L174] ▼ ▼ ▼ ▼ [L175] Tweets Quotes Images Clips Micro-content [L176] ``` [L177] [L178] ### Repurposing Workflow [L179] [L180] One blog post becomes: [L181] - Twitter thread [L182] - LinkedIn article [L183] - 5-10 individual tweets/posts [L184] - Newsletter section [L185] - Carousel graphics [L186] - Video script [L187] - Podcast talking points [L188] [L189] ### Repurposing Rules [L190] [L191] - Wait between platforms (not same day) [L192] - Adapt format to platform norms [L193] - Don't just copy/paste [L194] - Update with new insights [L195] [L196] --- [L197] [L198] ## Engagement Strategy [L199] [L200] ### Meaningful Engagement [L201] [L202] **Do**: [L203] - Add value to conversations [L204] - Ask genuine questions [L205] - Share relevant experiences [L206] - Credit and amplify others [L207] [L208] **Don't**: [L209] - Generic comments ("Great post!") [L210] - Hijack threads for self-promo [L211] - Engage only with big accounts [L212] - Automate engagement [L213] [L214] ### Building Relationships [L215] [L216] 1. **Identify peers**: 20-50 people in your space [L217] 2. **Engage consistently**: Comment on their work [L218] 3. **Add value first**: Help before asking [L219] 4. **Collaborate**: Guest posts, interviews, projects [L220] [L221] ### Responding to Engagement [L222] [L223] - Reply to comments within 24 hours [L224] - Ask follow-up questions [L225] - Thank people who share [L226] - DM people who engage consistently [L227] [L228] --- [L229] [L230] ## Analytics That Matter [L231] [L232] ### Vanity vs Valuable Metrics [L233] [L234] | Vanity | Valuable | [L235] |--------|----------| [L236] | Follower count | Follower growth rate | [L237] | Total likes | Engagement rate | [L238] | Impressions | Click-through rate | [L239] | Views | Subscribers/email signups | [L240] [L241] ### What to Track [L242] [L243] - Which content types perform best? [L244] - When does your audience engage? [L245] - What topics resonate? [L246] - Where do website visitors come from? [L247] [L248] ### Review Cadence [L249] [L250] - **Weekly**: Quick check on recent posts [L251] - **Monthly**: Content performance review [L252] - **Quarterly**: Strategy adjustment [L253] [L254] --- [L255] [L256] ## Sustainable Schedule [L257] [L258] ### Minimum Viable Presence [L259] [L260] | Platform | Minimum | Ideal | [L261] |----------|---------|-------| [L262] | Twitter | 3x/week | 1x/day | [L263] | LinkedIn | 2x/week | 3-4x/week | [L264] | Newsletter | 2x/month | Weekly | [L265] | Blog | 2x/month | Weekly | [L266] | YouTube | 2x/month | Weekly | [L267] [L268] ### Batching [L269] [L270] - **Write day**: Create content in batches [L271] - **Schedule ahead**: Use scheduling tools [L272] - **Repurpose day**: Transform existing content [L273] - **Engagement time**: Daily 15-30 min blocks [L274] [L275] --- [L276] [L277] ## Launch Strategy [L278] [L279] ### For a New Project [L280] [L281] **Pre-launch** (2-4 weeks before): [L282] - Tease what's coming [L283] - Share behind-the-scenes [L284] - Build email list interest [L285] [L286] **Launch week**: [L287] - Announce on all platforms [L288] - Ask friends to share [L289] - Engage with every comment [L290] - Share social proof [L291] [L292] **Post-launch**: [L293] - Thank supporters [L294] - Share results/learnings [L295] - Continue creating content [L296] [L297] --- [L298] [L299] ## References [L300] [L301] - `references/platform-guides.md` - Platform-specific tactics [L302] - `references/content-calendar-template.md` - Planning templates [L303] - `references/tools-stack.md` - Scheduling and analytics tools

Citation Marker: fileciteturn85file0 [L1] encoding: utf-8 [L2] sha: 0ba4a6a507d8eda244ddab29a15f14918f8c7447 [L3] content: [![ORGAN-I: Theory](https://img.shields.io/badge/ORGAN--I-Theory-1a237e?style=flat-square)](https://github.com/organvm-i-theoria) [L4] [![License: MIT](https://img.shields.io/badge/license-MIT-green?style=flat-square)](LICENSE) [L5] [![Status: Planning](https://img.shields.io/badge/status-planning-lightgrey?style=flat-square)]() [L6] [L7] # Collective Persona Operations [L8] [L9] [![CI](https://github.com/organvm-i-theoria/collective-persona-operations/actions/workflows/ci.yml/badge.svg)](https://github.com/organvm-i-theoria/collective-persona-operations/actions/workflows/ci.yml) [L10] [![Coverage](https://img.shields.io/badge/coverage-pending-lightgrey)](https://github.com/organvm-i-theoria/collective-persona-operations) [L11] [![License: MIT](https://img.shields.io/badge/License-MIT-blue.svg)](https://github.com/organvm-i-theoria/collective-persona-operations/blob/main/LICENSE) [L12] [![Organ I](https://img.shields.io/badge/Organ-I%20Theoria-8B5CF6)](https://github.com/organvm-i-theoria) [L13] [![Status](https://img.shields.io/badge/status-active-brightgreen)](https://github.com/organvm-i-theoria/collective-persona-operations) [L14] [![Markdown](https://img.shields.io/badge/lang-Markdown-informational)](https://github.com/organvm-i-theoria/collective-persona-operations) [L15] [L16] [L17] **A theoretical and operational framework for managing coherent identity across multi-agent systems, multi-organ institutions, and multi-register creative practices — treating persona not as performance but as a composable epistemic interface.** [L18] [L19] > "The self is not a point but a pattern of points." — Gregory Bateson [L20] [L21] --- [L22] [L23] ## Name Explanation [L24] [L25] **Collective Persona** refers to the many-as-one problem of identity: how does a single authorial intelligence present itself coherently when it operates through multiple agents, organisations, contexts, and registers? The "collective" is not a committee but a *field* — the unified identity that emerges from the coordination of distinct voices, just as a symphony emerges from instruments that are individually incomplete. **Operations** signals that this is not merely a philosophical inquiry. These are executable procedures: protocols, state machines, validation engines, and switching rules that can be implemented in code and enforced across a distributed creative-institutional system. [L26] [L27] The compound name positions the repo at the intersection of identity theory and systems engineering — exactly where ORGAN-I (Theoria) does its most distinctive work. [L28] [L29] --- [L30] [L31] ## Table of Contents [L32] [L33] - [Problem Statement](#problem-statement) [L34] - [Core Concepts](#core-concepts) [L35] - [Theoretical Framework](#theoretical-framework) [L36] - [Planned Architecture](#planned-architecture) [L37] - [Use Cases Within the Eight-Organ System](#use-cases-within-the-eight-organ-system) [L38] - [Related Work](#related-work) [L39] - [Roadmap](#roadmap) [L40] - [Cross-References](#cross-references) [L41] - [Contributing](#contributing) [L42] - [License](#license) [L43] - [Author & Contact](#author--contact) [L44] [L45] --- [L46] [L47] ## Problem Statement [L48] [L49] ### The Incoherence of Multi-Contextual Identity [L50] [L51] When a single creator operates across eight organisations, dozens of repositories, and multiple public-facing contexts — grant applications, open-source communities, commercial products, theoretical publications, public essays, marketing announcements — the question of *who is speaking* becomes non-trivial. Every context demands a different register: the academic rigour expected in a theory repo is not the conversational directness needed for a building-in-public essay; the commercial precision of a SaaS product page is not the experimental freedom of a generative art README. [L52] [L53] Most practitioners handle this by intuition. They "code-switch" between registers unconsciously, the way a bilingual person shifts between languages depending on who they are speaking to. This works at small scale. It fails catastrophically when: [L54] [L55] 1. **AI agents enter the workflow.** An LLM generating a README for ORGAN-III (Commerce) has no inherent knowledge that its voice should differ from the one used in ORGAN-I (Theory). Without explicit persona specifications, AI-generated content trends toward a flat, generic register that belongs nowhere and convinces no one. [L56] [L57] 2. **The system scales beyond one person's memory.** A single author can hold eight distinct voices in their head. A team cannot. A multi-agent system certainly cannot. Without formalisation, persona coherence degrades as the system grows. [L58] [L59] 3. **Cross-organ content creates identity conflicts.** When an ORGAN-V (Logos) essay quotes an ORGAN-I (Theoria) concept, the citation must bridge two registers without breaking either. When ORGAN-VII (Kerygma) announces a product from ORGAN-III (Ergon), the marketing voice must amplify the commercial voice without distorting it. These cross-organ interactions are where incoherence becomes visible. [L60] [L61] 4. **External audiences enforce judgment.** A grant reviewer reading both a theoretical paper and a product pitch from the same author expects *consistency without uniformity*. A hiring manager scanning READMEs across multiple repos expects a recognisable authorial presence. Incoherence reads as carelessness or, worse, as inauthenticity. [L62] [L63] ### Why Existing Frameworks Fail [L64] [L65] Current approaches to identity in multi-agent systems fall into two inadequate categories: [L66] [L67] - **Role-Based Access Control (RBAC) / Identity Management.** These systems answer "who has permission to do what?" — not "who is speaking and how?" They manage authentication and authorisation, not voice and register. A persona is not a role; it is an expressive mode. [L68] [L69] - **Brand Guidelines / Style Guides.** These are static documents: "use this font, this colour palette, this tone of voice." They describe the *output* of persona coherence but not the *mechanism*. They cannot adapt to context, validate outputs, or compose across multiple registers. A style guide tells you what the voice should sound like; it does not tell the system how to produce it. [L70] [L71] What is missing is a **dynamic, composable, machine-readable persona layer** — one that sits between the raw content generation capabilities of AI agents and the contextual requirements of specific organs, audiences, and publication contexts. Collective Persona Operations is the theoretical foundation and operational specification for that layer. [L72] [L73] --- [L74] [L75] ## Core Concepts [L76] [L77] ### 1. Persona as Interface [L78] [L79] The central theoretical move is to treat persona not as a mask (the theatrical metaphor) or as a role (the sociological metaphor) but as an **interface** in the software engineering sense: a contract that specifies how a system presents itself to a given context while hiding the complexity of its internal state. [L80] [L81] An interface defines: [L82] - **What is exposed** — the public methods, the observable behaviour [L83] - **What is hidden** — the implementation details, the internal contradictions [L84] - **What is guaranteed** — the invariants that callers can rely on [L85] [L86] A persona-as-interface defines: [L87] - **What voice is exposed** — register, vocabulary, tone, rhetorical patterns [L88] - **What is hidden** — the machinery of the other organs, the cross-organ dependencies, the personal biography that does not belong in this context [L89] - **What is guaranteed** — consistency within the register, traceability to the unified authorial identity, absence of contradictions with other persona instances [L90] [L91] This reframing transforms persona management from a creative-writing problem into a systems-engineering problem with formal properties that can be specified, validated, and tested. [L92] [L93] ### 2. The Persona Registry [L94] [L95] Every persona in the system is a first-class entity with a formal specification. The **Persona Registry** is a structured catalogue of all active personas, each defined by: [L96] [L97] | Field | Description | [L98] |-------|-------------| [L99] | `id` | Unique identifier (e.g., `organ-i-theoretical`, `organ-iii-commercial`) | [L100] | `register` | The linguistic register (academic, conversational, commercial, artistic, etc.) | [L101] | `vocabulary_constraints` | Words and phrases that are encouraged, discouraged, or prohibited | [L102] | `rhetorical_patterns` | Preferred argument structures (deductive, narrative, exemplary, etc.) | [L103] | `audience_model` | Who this persona addresses (grant reviewers, developers, general public, etc.) | [L104] | `temperature` | Metaphorical: how experimental or conservative the voice is | [L105] | `lineage` | Which other personas this one inherits from or contrasts with | [L106] | `context_rules` | When this persona activates (org, repo type, document type, audience) | [L107] [L108] The registry is the single source of truth for persona state, analogous to `registry-v2.json` for repository state. [L109] [L110] ### 3. Identity Composability [L111] [L112] Personas are not monolithic. They compose. The voice used in a cross-organ document — say, an ORGAN-V essay that discusses ORGAN-I theory and announces an ORGAN-III product — is not a fourth persona but a *composition* of three, governed by explicit rules: [L113] [L114] - **Dominance hierarchy:** Which persona leads? (In ORGAN-V, the essay voice dominates; the others are quoted.) [L115] - **Blending rules:** How do registers merge? (Academic vocabulary can appear in an essay voice; commercial jargon cannot.) [L116] - **Boundary markers:** How does the text signal transitions? (Quotation, section breaks, register shifts.) [L117] [L118] Composability is what distinguishes this framework from a simple style guide. A style guide says "use this voice." A composable persona system says "given these three voices and this context, here is how they combine, and here are the invariants that must hold." [L119] [L120] ### 4. Persona Switching as State Machine [L121] [L122] Context switching between personas is modeled as a finite state machine. Each persona is a state; transitions are triggered by context changes (different org, different document type, different audience). The state machine enforces: [L123] [L124] - **No illegal transitions:** You cannot jump from the commercial register to the artistic register without passing through a neutral state. This prevents jarring tonal shifts. [L125] - **Transition costs:** Some switches are cheap (theoretical → academic) because the registers are adjacent. Others are expensive (commercial → artistic) because the registers are distant. Cost maps to the editorial effort required. [L126] - **Hysteresis:** Once in a persona state, the system resists switching. This prevents the "wandering voice" problem where a document drifts between registers without committing to any. [L127] [L128] ### 5. Voice Consistency Validation [L129] [L130] The operational counterpart of persona theory is **validation**: given a document and its declared persona, does the document actually conform? Validation operates at multiple levels: [L131] [L132] - **Lexical:** Does the vocabulary match the register? (Academic persona should not use marketing superlatives; commercial persona should not use jargon unexplained.) [L133] - **Structural:** Does the argument structure match the rhetorical pattern? (Deductive personas lead with premises; narrative personas lead with anecdotes.) [L134] - **Relational:** Does this document's voice relate correctly to sibling documents in the same organ and cousin documents in other organs? [L135] [L136] Validation can be partially automated through NLP techniques (readability scoring, vocabulary analysis, rhetorical structure detection) and partially through human review guided by checklists derived from the persona specification. [L137] [L138] --- [L139] [L140] ## Theoretical Framework [L141] [L142] ### Philosophy of Personal Identity [L143] [L144] The Western philosophical tradition on identity runs from Locke's memory criterion (you are your memories) through Hume's bundle theory (there is no self, only a bundle of perceptions) to Parfit's reductionism (personal identity is not what matters; what matters is psychological continuity). Collective Persona Operations draws most directly from **narrative identity theory** (Ricoeur, MacIntyre): the self is constituted by the stories it tells about itself, and coherence is achieved not through metaphysical unity but through narrative consistency. [L145] [L146] In the multi-organ context, the "narrative" is the corpus of all published artifacts — READMEs, essays, product pages, code comments — and "consistency" means that a reader encountering any subset of these artifacts would recognise a single authorial intelligence operating in context-appropriate registers. [L147] [L148] ### Collective Intelligence and Multi-Agent Systems [L149] [L150] From the multi-agent systems literature (Woolley et al., 2010; Malone & Bernstein, 2015), we borrow the concept of **collective intelligence factors**: the properties that make a group smarter than its individual members. In our context, the "group" is not a team of humans but a constellation of AI agents, each generating content for a different organ. The collective intelligence factor is the persona coherence layer: the system that ensures the agents' outputs combine into a coherent institutional identity rather than a cacophony of unrelated voices. [L151] [L152] This connects directly to the work in `a-recursive-root` (the AI Council system), where multiple agent archetypes engage in structured deliberation. The AI Council produces *decisions*; Collective Persona Operations produces *voices*. They are complementary: the Council determines what to say, and the Persona system determines how to say it in each context. [L153] [L154] ### Erving Goffman and Dramaturgical Analysis [L155] [L156] Goffman's *The Presentation of Self in Everyday Life* (1956) introduced the theatrical metaphor for social interaction: we perform different "selves" in different contexts (front stage vs. back stage). This framework has obvious relevance, but we depart from Goffman on a critical point. For Goffman, the performed self is a *deception* — a managed impression that conceals the "true" self. In our framework, there is no "true" self behind the personas. The personas are the self, or more precisely, the self is the *coherence function* that relates the personas to each other. The backstage is not a hidden reality; it is the governance layer that ensures the front-stage performances are mutually consistent. [L157] [L158] This is not relativism. It is engineering. A software system that presents different APIs to different clients is not "deceiving" anyone; it is providing context-appropriate interfaces to a single underlying system. Collective Persona Operations treats the author the same way. [L159] [L160] --- [L161] [L162] ## Planned Architecture [L163] [L164] Since this repository is in the planning stage, the architecture described here is the intended design. Implementation will follow as the eight-organ system matures and generates the practical demand for persona coordination tooling. [L165] [L166] ``` [L167] ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────┐ [L168] │ Persona Governance Layer │ [L169] │ │ [L170] │ ┌──────────┐ ┌──────────┐ ┌───────────────┐ │ [L171] │ │ Persona │ │ Context │ │ Composition │ │ [L172] │ │ Registry │ │ Detector │ │ Engine │ │ [L173] │ └────┬─────┘ └────┬─────┘ └───────┬───────┘ │ [L174] │ │ │ │ │ [L175] │ ▼ ▼ ▼ │ [L176] │ ┌──────────────────────────────────────────┐ │ [L177] │ │ Persona State Machine │ │ [L178] │ │ (current state, legal transitions, │ │ [L179] │ │ hysteresis parameters) │ │ [L180] │ └────────────────────┬─────────────────────┘ │ [L181] │ │ │ [L182] │ ┌────────────────────▼─────────────────────┐ │ [L183] │ │ Voice Consistency Validator │ │ [L184] │ │ (lexical, structural, relational) │ │ [L185] │ └──────────────────────────────────────────┘ │ [L186] └─────────────────────────────────────────────────┘ [L187] │ │ [L188] ▼ ▼ [L189] ┌───────────┐ ┌────────────┐ [L190] │ AI Agent │ │ Human │ [L191] │ Prompts │ │ Review │ [L192] │ (system │ │ Checklists│ [L193] │... Citation Marker: fileciteturn86file0 [L1] encoding: utf-8 [L2] sha: 79e72727d39c6766d3b94dffe173bc1639414af7 [L3] content: [![ORGAN-III: Ergon](https://img.shields.io/badge/ORGAN--III-Ergon-1b5e20?style=flat-square)](https://github.com/organvm-iii-ergon) [L4] [![TypeScript](https://img.shields.io/badge/TypeScript-5.7-3178c6?style=flat-square&logo=typescript&logoColor=white)](https://www.typescriptlang.org/) [L5] [![React](https://img.shields.io/badge/React-19-61dafb?style=flat-square&logo=react&logoColor=black)](https://react.dev/) [L6] [![License: MIT](https://img.shields.io/badge/License-MIT-yellow?style=flat-square)](./LICENSE) [L7] [![Vite](https://img.shields.io/badge/Vite-7-646cff?style=flat-square&logo=vite&logoColor=white)](https://vite.dev/) [L8] [L9] # Aerarium (formerly The Invisible Ledger) [L10] [L11] **The deployable family office: institutional weight for one person, zero staff.** [L12] [L13] *Aerarium is built from the-invisible-ledger's accounting core, scaled from a B2B CPA tool into a personal financial operating system.* [L14] [L15] A billionaire's family office does not have a smarter principal; it has more bench. Behind every ultra-high-net-worth individual stands a coordinated team — CPAs, tax strategists, investment analysts, bill-pay clerks, estate planners, and a CFO who connects the pieces. [L16] [L17] This platform gives one person the infrastructure of a billionaire's family office: a continuously reconciled, always-current, projection-capable view of their entire financial position, with AI roles that do what a CPO, tax strategist, analyst, and bill-pay clerk would do — without the machine ever touching the money itself. [L18] [L19] **Intake is owned by MONETA (`moneta/`), the sovereign cash organ.** Aerarium tracks the institution around it. MONETA is the rail. [L20] [L21] --- [L22] [L23] ## What It Is [L24] [L25] Aerarium is a **deployable family office** — the institutional prosthesis a billionaire buys with a $500K+/year staff, delivered as a directory of structured files and a generator that keeps them current, paired with this React-based operations dashboard. [L26] [L27] The platform turns scattered financial facts into one operating surface: [L28] [L29] - **Entity registry:** people, LLCs, nonprofits, trusts, products, wallets, accounts, and obligations registered as first-class financial members. [L30] - **Consolidated balance sheet:** assets and liabilities roll up across every entity, with unknown balances explicitly marked instead of hidden (no fake zeros). [L31] - **Rolling cash-flow projection:** known inflows, obligations, runway, and reserve needs rebuilt on every beat. [L32] - **Payrail disbursement map:** money paths modeled from revenue source to collection account to entity account to obligation, with the gate and tax treatment for each hop. [L33] - **Tax-position desk:** estimated liabilities, installments, filing windows, deductions, and CPA handoff packets staged from the same ledger. [L34] - **Compliance sentinel:** every output checked for source timestamp, approval gate, segregation of duties, assumption labels, and policy limits. [L35] [L36] ## The Boundary with MONETA [L37] [L38] MONETA (moneta/) is the sovereign cash rail. It intakes value (BTC), holds no spending keys, reads the public chain, and mints product licenses. [L39] Aerarium (this repo + limen organs/financial) is the financial office. It tracks the institution, holds no credentials, reads file-backed entity data, and generates dashboards. [L40] [L41] MONETA records a receipt ──→ Aerarium logs it as revenue ──→ Aerarium updates cash-flow ──→ Principal executes transfers. [L42] [L43] ## Pricing and Monetization [L44] [L45] The buyer is the firm or family office, not the firm's clients. The current go-to-market path is documented in [docs/PRICING.md](./docs/PRICING.md): a $199 / firm / month base offer, a 14-day no-card trial, and custom-quoted air-gap or multi-organization deployments. [L46] [L47] For serious buyers, the useful next action is a scoped deployment request: describe the firm size, privacy tier, document intake volume, ShareFile or storage stack, and whether an air-gapped workflow is required. For maintainers, new revenue-repo work should first pass the [revenue waste triage](./docs/REVENUE_WASTE_TRIAGE.md) rule so public activity creates a buyer-facing proof surface instead of feature churn. [L48] [L49] ## Architecture [L50] [L51] Aerarium runs a client-side React 19 application built on Vite. It visualizes the artifacts generated by the `limen` financial organ's `consolidate.py`. [L52] [L53] ## Usage [L54] [L55] ### Run Locally [L56] [L57] ```bash [L58] npm ci [L59] npm run dev # Vite dev server with HMR on http://localhost:5000 [L60] ``` [L61] [L62] ### Build for Production [L63] [L64] ```bash [L65] npm run build # TypeScript project build + Vite production bundle [L66] npm run preview # Serve dist/ locally [L67] ``` [L68] [L69] ### Test and Lint [L70] [L71] ```bash [L72] npm run test # Vitest run [L73] npm run lint # ESLint across the project [L74] npm run typecheck # TypeScript check without emitting files [L75] ``` [L76] [L77] ### Auth CLI [L78] [L79] The API-key CLI manages HMAC-hashed key records stored in `.ledger-auth/api-keys.json`. [L80] It requires `THE_INVISIBLE_LEDGER_API_KEY_SECRET`; raw keys are only printed at issuance. [L81] [L82] ```bash [L83] npm run auth:issue -- \ [L84] --subject <name> \ [L85] --scope <scope> [--scope <scope>] \ [L86] [--environment live|test] \ [L87] [--expires-at <ISO-8601 date>] [L88] [L89] npm run auth:verify -- --key <api-key> [--scope <required-scope>] [L90] THE_INVISIBLE_LEDGER_API_KEY=<key> npm run auth:verify -- [--scope <scope>] [L91] [L92] npm run auth:revoke -- --id <key-id> [L93] npm run auth:list [L94] ``` [L95] [L96] ### Docker and Deploy [L97] [L98] ```bash [L99] npm run docker:build [L100] npm run docker:run [L101] npm run deploy [L102] PORT=3000 npm run deploy [L103] ``` [L104] [L105] ### Revenue Triage [L106] [L107] ```bash [L108] npm run triage:revenue -- --ledger <path-to-ledger.json> --repo organvm/the-invisible-ledger [L109] ``` [L110] [L111] Use this before opening more value-tier work on the repo. It turns aggregate waste signals into a narrow buyer-facing next action without committing private Limen ledger data. [L112] [L113] ## Contributing [L114] Aerarium is an ORGAN-III (Ergon) project, scaling the invisible ledger architecture to personal sovereign finance.

Citation Marker: fileciteturn87file0 [L1] encoding: utf-8 [L2] sha: 4978b69a332474a534b41e7486c65c19e99d74ed [L3] content: # Materia Collider [L4] [L5] A film-scrubbing system for the AMP Lab / Object Lessons production pipeline. [L6] [L7] Object Lessons compiles clips of recurring objects across 100 years of cinema -- a single episode covers 50-70 films for one object (milk, telephones, cigarettes). The bottleneck is research: manually scrubbing through films to find where objects appear, logging timestamps, extracting clips, and tracking what has been used. Materia Collider replaces the spreadsheet/notes workflow with a structured, searchable clip database and CLI. [L8] [L9] ## MVP Scope (Phase 1) [L10] [L11] Manual clip extraction with a structured database. No object detection yet -- the operator timestamps clips as before, but stores everything in a queryable SQLite database. [L12] [L13] What this unlocks: [L14] - Every clip ever found is searchable [L15] - Episode assembly goes from "scroll through notes" to "query the database" [L16] - Coverage gaps become visible (missing decades, underrepresented directors) [L17] - Content ID history accumulates across episodes [L18] [L19] ## Installation [L20] [L21] ```bash [L22] pip install -e ".[dev]" [L23] ``` [L24] [L25] ## Quick Start [L26] [L27] ```bash [L28] # Register a film [L29] materia ingest "/media/films/Psycho (1960).mkv" [L30] [L31] # Add an object to track [L32] materia object add milk --category food --alias "glass of milk" --alias "milk bottle" [L33] [L34] # Add a clip (manual timestamp entry) [L35] materia clip add 1 milk 120.0 128.5 --scene-type dialogue --valence "domesticity, maternal control" [L36] [L37] # Search across all clips [L38] materia search milk [L39] materia search milk --director "Hitchcock" --year-min 1950 --year-max 1970 [L40] [L41] # Assemble a rough cut timeline [L42] materia assemble milk --gaps [L43] materia assemble milk --export edl --output milk-rough.edl [L44] [L45] # Database statistics [L46] materia stats [L47] ``` [L48] [L49] ## CLI Reference [L50] [L51] ``` [L52] materia ingest <path> # Register a film [L53] materia films # List all films [L54] [L55] materia object add <name> [--category X] # Add an object to track [L56] materia objects # List all objects [L57] [L58] materia clip add <film_id> <object> <start> <end> # Add a clip [L59] materia clips [object] [--film-id X] # List clips [L60] [L61] materia search <query> [--director X] # Full-text search [L62] materia assemble <object> [--order chronological|director|thematic] [--gaps] [L63] materia export <object> --format edl|csv|markdown [L64] materia stats # Database statistics [L65] ``` [L66] [L67] ## Data Storage [L68] [L69] The database and extracted media live outside the repository: [L70] [L71] ``` [L72] ~/.materia/ # Default ($MATERIA_DATA_DIR overrides) [L73] materia.db # SQLite database (metadata only, <50 MB for 500 films) [L74] ``` [L75] [L76] ## Future Phases [L77] [L78] **Phase 2 -- Semi-Automated Detection:** YOLOv8-nano object detection with human review. A 2-hour film goes from 2-3 hours of manual scrubbing to ~2 minutes of detection + 10-20 minutes of review. [L79] [L80] **Phase 3 -- Full Automation:** Fine-tuned model trained on Object Lessons back-catalog as ground truth. CLIP-based semantic search. Batch processing of entire media libraries overnight. [L81] [L82] See `praxis-perpetua/specifications/2026-03-19-film-scrubbing-system-spec.md` for the full spec. [L83] [L84] ## Pre-Codified Space [L85] [L86] This repo also contains the original materia-collider idea space -- protocols, bench notes, experiments, and observations from before the film-scrubbing system was codified. See `genesis/`, `protocols/`, `bench/`, `experiments/`, and `observations/` for that material.

```unknown from __future__ import annotations from pathlib import Path import csv import json import textwrap import zipfile import yaml root = Path("/mnt/data/podcast_os_github_recomposition") root.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True) blueprint = """\ # Podcast / Conversation OS — GitHub Recomposition Blueprint **Status:** Architecture audit; no repository mutations performed **Working product name:** Conversation Operations System **Primary proof environments:** Ari + Anthony flagship show; Anthony's mobile field show **Commercial direction:** Multi-tenant invisible production desk for podcasters and studio networks ## Executive conclusion This is not a greenfield build. The existing GitHub estate already contains most of the *horizontal machinery* required for a serious podcast operating system: - relationship CRM and weak-tie pathfinding - guest/opportunity pipeline mechanics - inbox triage, follow-up aging, draft approvals, and audit trails - booking and reminder interaction patterns - multi-camera capture profiles and production runbooks - canonical media ingestion, deduplication, metadata, and archival integrity - transcript atomization, speaker/timestamp export, semantic analysis, and clip assembly - editorial standards, episode production templates, and object-driven segment logic - content fragmentation and platform-specific asset generation - distribution dispatch, retries, receipts, and analytics - voice/persona registries and deterministic style validation - human-in-the-loop agent orchestration - evidence-linked publishing and correction gates The missing product is not another agent. It is a **podcast-specific domain kernel and composition boundary** that turns these systems into one coherent product. ## Governing architecture decision Do **not** physically merge every repository into one giant codebase. Use three modes of reuse: 1. **Retain as service** — mature systems keep their identity and expose a stable adapter. 2. **Extract as package** — portable logic moves into a shared package with provenance back to its source. 3. **Adapt as specification** — schemas, rubrics, workflows, and creative methods become podcast-domain configuration. 4. **Archive as precursor** — superseded or duplicate surfaces are preserved and redirected; nothing unique is destroyed. ## Canonical domain kernel The central entity is **AppearanceOpportunity**, not `Guest` and not `Lead`. A person can decline one opportunity, accept another, return years later, appear on multiple shows, or be represented through different routes. The system must preserve that distinction. ### Core entities - `Tenant` - `Network` - `Show` - `Host` - `Person` - `Organization` - `ContactRoute` - `Relationship` - `RelationshipEdge` - `AppearanceOpportunity` - `Episode` - `Studio` - `AvailabilityWindow` - `Booking` - `Touchpoint` - `Commitment` - `ConsentRecord` - `GuestCareProfile` - `ResearchClaim` - `EvidenceObject` - `Segment` - `Artifact` - `MediaAsset` - `TranscriptSegment` - `ContentUnit` - `DistributionJob` - `SponsorCampaign` - `ApprovalRequest` - `AuditEvent` ### Appearance state machine ```text DISCOVERED → RESEARCHING → QUALIFIED → EDITORIAL_REVIEW → APPROVED → CONTACT_ROUTE_IDENTIFIED → OUTREACH_DRAFTED → OUTREACH_APPROVED → OUTREACH_SENT → INTERESTED → SCHEDULING → BOOKED → INTAKE_PENDING → RELEASE_PENDING → PREP_IN_PROGRESS → RECORDING_READY → RECORDED → TRANSCRIPT_READY → CONTENT_IN_REVIEW → PUBLICATION_PENDING → PUBLISHED → RELATIONSHIP_NURTURE ``` Branch states: ```text FOLLOW_UP_DUE REVISIT_LATER DECLINED DO_NOT_CONTACT PROTECTED_RELATIONSHIP LEGAL_REVIEW NEEDS_HUMAN CANCELLED ``` ## Target product architecture ```text conversation-ops/ ├── apps/ │ ├── operator/ # Ari/producer approvals and exception queue │ ├── guest-portal/ # scheduling, intake, releases, care preferences │ ├── show-console/ # episode thesis, research, segments, day-of packet │ ├── network-admin/ # multi-tenant setup, studios, shows, policies │ └── field-capture/ # Anthony's portable show profile and ingest ├── services/ │ ├── api/ │ ├── workflow-worker/ │ ├── mail-ingestor/ │ ├── calendar-router/ │ ├── media-ingestor/ │ ├── transcript-worker/ │ ├── content-worker/ │ └── distribution-worker/ ├── packages/ │ ├── domain/ │ ├── database/ │ ├── events/ │ ├── policy/ │ ├── approvals/ │ ├── network-graph/ │ ├── voice/ │ ├── editorial/ │ ├── capture-profiles/ │ ├── integrations/ │ └── observability/ └── show-profiles/ ├── flagship/ └── field-show/ ``` ## Source-to-target composition ### Retain as services #### `content-engine--asset-amplifier` Owns derivative generation after a master recording is approved: - clip extraction - fragment scoring - captions and platform variants - resizing - approval states - scheduled release - yield analytics **Boundary:** It does not own canonical raw media or guest relationships. #### `universal-mail--automation` Owns inbox ingestion and correspondence workflow: - thread ingestion - classification - escalation - follow-up aging - draft approvals - delivery evidence - privacy and redaction controls **Boundary:** Podcast-specific intent classes and relationship permissions live in Conversation OS. #### `media-ark` Owns canonical source media: - ingest - hashes - deduplication - sidecars - metadata - archive verification - repair **Boundary:** Content Engine may read masters and write derivatives, but it must not become the archive of record. #### `social-automation` Owns channel dispatch mechanics: - platform adapters - retries - circuit breakers - delivery receipts - distribution analytics **Boundary:** Announcement templates and Content Engine create payloads; Social Automation delivers them. ### Extract as packages #### From `application-pipeline` Extract: - opportunity state-machine patterns - scoring framework - funnel and velocity analytics - relationship CRM semantics - next-action and overdue-action logic - weak-tie graph and pathfinding - network-proximity scoring Replace job-specific terms with: - `application` → `appearance_opportunity` - `organization target` → `guest / representative / institution` - `interview` → `recording` - `outcome` → `booked / declined / revisit / published` #### From `public-record-data-scrapper` Extract: - production-grade multi-tenant contact service - contact activity ledger - many-to-many contact associations - timezone, preferred contact method, tags, source provenance - API, PostgreSQL, Redis, workers, OpenAPI, auth patterns Do **not** reuse the public-record scraping purpose or lead language. #### From `vox--architectura-gubernatio` and `vox--publica` Extract: - persona/voice registry - anti-pattern detectors - output linting - human approval queue - corpus comparison Create separate voice profiles for: - Ari personal note - producer / guest desk - flagship show - Anthony field show - sponsor creative - public launch copy #### From `agentic-titan` Extract: - approval gates - audit event format - bounded tool permissions - budget controls - model routing - workflow DAG patterns Do not import a free-roaming 22-agent swarm. Start with deterministic workflows and five bounded capabilities. #### From `mirror-mirror` Extract: - booking UX - slot-ranking preference schema - confirmation flow - reminder data model - retry concepts - operator dashboard patterns - group booking patterns - calendar export UX Rewrite: - mocked availability → Google Calendar free/busy + studio inventory - browser interval scheduler → durable server-side workflow - Spark KV → PostgreSQL - hard-coded providers → hosts, guests, producers, studios #### From `linguistic-atomization-framework` Extract: - transcript hierarchy - semantic and temporal analysis - entity extraction - sentiment/emotional trajectory - chapter and quote candidates - rhetorical and contradiction analysis #### From `materia-collider` Extract: - time-coded clip database - searchable clip annotations - coverage-gap reporting - rough-cut assembly - EDL/CSV/Markdown export - usage and rights history ### Adapt as podcast-domain specifications #### `salon-archive` Adapt: - session metadata - participants and consent - transcript review - topic taxonomy - outputs/artifacts - participant and topic indices - redaction and off-record rules This becomes the Conversation Archive and Episode Knowledge Graph. #### `praxis-perpetua` + `object-lessons` Adapt: - pre-production checklists - episode structure - clip logs - research briefs - SEO and thumbnail gates - Shorts extraction plans - performance review - lessons learned - object-driven episode and segment mechanics #### `editorial-standards` Adapt: - document types - required frontmatter - controlled vocabulary - review rubrics - metadata gates Create canonical documents: - guest dossier - appearance brief - episode thesis - segment card - day-of packet - sponsor brief - publication package - postmortem #### `announcement-templates` Adapt: - single source → multiple channel outputs - variable interpolation - channel-specific formatting - factual consistency - publication checklists #### `the-actual-news` Adapt: - atomic claim/evidence linkage - provenance records - deterministic publish gate - immutable corrections - public/internal boundary - share-kit and offer-packet surfaces Use this for: - “Receipts” segments - guest research claims - ad claims - sponsor approvals - corrections to show notes and metadata #### `collective-persona-operations` Adapt: - persona as machine-readable interface - context-sensitive register - composition rules - legal persona transitions - voice consistency validation #### `a-i--skills` Adapt: - relational, give-first outreach - research-before-contact - connector strategy - concise email structures - distribution and repurposing methods Do not inherit generic sequences blindly. The show’s policy should override them. ### Preserve as creative/R&D layers #### `speech-score-engine` Use later for: - host/guest turn-duration diagnostics - interruption and overlap analysis - pacing drag - rhythm monotony - ad-sketch timing - polyvocal segment design It is not a core dependency for launch. #### `sign-signal--voice-synth` Preserve as the conceptual precursor to Speech Score Engine. Redirect new implementation work to the latter. #### `meta-source--ledger-output` Optional visual layer for: - episode glyphs - kinetic interstitials - diagrams - generative identity - artifact rendering ### Archive or fold as independent active surfaces These should not remain competing product centers unless deeper implementation justifies it: - `kerygma-pipeline` → fold into distribution orchestration - duplicate or precursor content-engine surfaces → preserve history, redirect to Asset Amplifier - `universal-node-network` → retain specification; defer runtime adoption until needed - `sign-signal--voice-synth` → preserve source corpus, redirect to Speech Score Engine “No longer an active product surface” does not mean deletion. ## The five bounded AI capabilities 1. **Guest Intelligence** - source candidates - build dossiers - map representatives and relationship routes - score editorial fit and social cost 2. **Booking Desk** - draft outreach - classify replies - manage follow-up policy - route exceptions to humans 3. **Scheduling and Guest Experience** - studio/host/guest availability - intake and releases - accessibility and care preferences - reminders and logistics 4. **Episode Producer** - research claims and evidence - thesis and segment design - host brief - day-of packet - transcript and artifact extraction 5. **Relationship and Distribution Steward** - thank-you and commitments - publication notifications - content package - dispatch and analytics - long-term relationship state ## Event vocabulary ```text person.created relationship.edge_created relationship.protected appearance.candidate_created appearance.qualified appearance.approved contact_route.verified outreach.draft_ready outreach.approved outreach.sent reply.received reply.classified followup.due booking.proposed booking.confirmed booking.rescheduled consent.signed guest_intake.completed episode.thesis_locked research.claim_verified recording.ready recording.completed media.ingested transcript.ready segment.identified commitment.created commitment.completed content_unit.generated content_unit.approved distribution.dispatched distribution.delivered episode.published correction.appended relationship.followup_due ``` ## Multi-tenant product model Because the same system must support two internal shows and later outside podcasters, multi-tenancy is not a later feature. ```text Network / Customer ├── Show │ ├── Show DNA │ ├── host roles │ ├── voice profiles │ ├── relationship policy │ ├── segment library │ ├── studio access │ ├── distribution policy │ └── sponsor policy ├── People and contact routes ├── protected relationship graph ├── assets and transcripts └── audit and approvals ``` A guest relationship may be network-level, but permission to use it must be explicit per show. ## Two initial show profiles ### Flagship - controlled studio environment - LA / NYC / Austin routing - hidden microphones - stable visual grammar - fixed and rotating segments - claim → stress test → artifact - Ari’s effort concentrated in approval and recording ### Anthony field show - portable GoPro/capture kit - guest environment as third participant - place → object → intervention → artifact - same guest desk, relationship graph, archive, and distribution system - different Show DNA and visual protocol ## Build order ### 0. Add advanced creative intelligence - speech rhythm diagnostics - overlap and interruption analysis - generative visual artifacts - adaptive segment scoring - ad-format experimentation ## Immediate repository work items 1. Write ADRs for: - service vs. package boundaries - canonical media ownership - contact/relationship ownership - workflow engine - multi-tenancy - evidence and correction policy 4. Build adapters before rewrites. 5. Replace mock scheduling with real calendar infrastructure. 6. Install a second internal tenant for the field show. 9. Only then install a third tenant for an outside podcaster. ## Product statement > An invisible guest, production, and distribution desk for podcasters: it turns a host’s relationships, studios, recordings, and editorial instincts into a governed operating system while keeping consequential decisions human. ## What is genuinely new The new value does not come from claiming that all prior repositories were secretly one podcast app. It comes from recognizing that they form a reusable institutional stack and adding the missing composition: - one podcast-domain ontology - one permissioned relationship graph - one deterministic appearance lifecycle - one multi-show control plane - one evidence-backed editorial layer - one governed path from candidate to relationship to recording to archive to distribution That composition is the product.
